The [Duchy of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw), a small, semi-independent Polish state, was created in 1807 by [Napoleon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon) in the wake of his defeat of Prussia and the signing of the [Treaties of Tilsit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit) with Emperor [Alexander I of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia).[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) The [Army of the Duchy of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_the_Duchy_of_Warsaw), led by [Józef Poniatowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Poniatowski), participated in numerous campaigns in alliance with France, including the successful [Austro-Polish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Polish_War) of 1809, which, combined with the outcomes of other theaters of the [War of the Fifth Coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition), resulted in an enlargement of the duchy's territory. The [French invasion of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia) in 1812 and the [German Campaign of 1813](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Campaign_of_1813) saw the duchy's last military engagements. The [Constitution of the Duchy of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Duchy_of_Warsaw) abolished serfdom as a reflection of the ideals of the [French Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Revolution), but it did not promote [land reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_reform).[[55\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_130–147-55)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Granting_of_the_Constitution_of_the_Duchy_of_Warsaw_by_Napoleon.PNG/220px-Granting_of_the_Constitution_of_the_Duchy_of_Warsaw_by_Napoleon.PNG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Granting_of_the_Constitution_of_the_Duchy_of_Warsaw_by_Napoleon.PNG)

[Napoleon Bonaparte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte) establishing the [Duchy of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw) under French protection, 1807

#### The Congress of Vienna

After Napoleon's defeat, a new European order was established at the [Congress of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna), which met in the years 1814 and 1815. [Adam Jerzy Czartoryski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Jerzy_Czartoryski), a former close associate of Emperor Alexander I, became the leading advocate for the [Polish national cause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_question). The Congress implemented a new partition scheme, which took into account some of the gains realized by the Poles during the Napoleonic period.

The Duchy of Warsaw was replaced in 1815 with a new Kingdom of Poland, unofficially known as [Congress Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_Poland).[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) The residual Polish kingdom was joined to the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire) in a [personal union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_union) under the Russian [tsar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsar) and it was allowed [its own constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland) and [military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Congress_Poland). East of the kingdom, large areas of the former Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth remained directly incorporated into the Russian Empire as the [Western Krai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Krai). These territories, along with Congress Poland, are generally considered to form the [Russian Partition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Partition). The Russian, Prussian, and Austrian "partitions" are informal names for the lands of the former Commonwealth, not actual units of [administrative division of Polish–Lithuanian territories after partitions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_division_of_Polish–Lithuanian_territories_after_partitions).[[56\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_147–181-56) The [Prussian Partition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_Partition) included a portion separated as the [Grand Duchy of Posen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Posen).[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) Peasants under the Prussian administration were gradually [enfranchised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffrage) under the reforms of 1811 and 1823. The limited legal reforms in the [Austrian Partition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Partition) were overshadowed by [its rural poverty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_in_Austrian_Galicia). The [Free City of Cracow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_City_of_Cracow) was a tiny republic created by the Congress of Vienna under the joint supervision of the three partitioning powers.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) Despite the bleak from the standpoint of Polish patriots political situation, economic progress was made in the lands taken over by foreign powers because the period after the Congress of Vienna witnessed a significant development in the building of early industry.[[56\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_147–181-56)

Economic historians have made new estimates on GDP per capita, 1790–1910. They confirm the hypothesis of semi-peripheral development of Polish territories in the 19th century and the slow process of catching-up with the core economies.[[57\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-57)

#### The Uprising of November 1830

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Marcin_Zaleski%2C_Wzi%C4%99cie_Arsena%C5%82u.jpg/220px-Marcin_Zaleski%2C_Wzi%C4%99cie_Arsena%C5%82u.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Marcin_Zaleski,_Wzięcie_Arsenału.jpg)

The capture of the Warsaw arsenal at the beginning of the [November Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/November_Uprising) of 1830

The increasingly repressive policies of the partitioning powers led to [resistance movements in partitioned Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resistance_movements_in_partitioned_Poland_(1795–1918)), and in 1830 Polish patriots staged the [November Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/November_Uprising).[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) This revolt developed into a full-scale war with Russia, but the leadership was taken over by Polish conservatives who were reluctant to challenge the empire and hostile to broadening the independence movement's social base through measures such as land reform. Despite the significant resources mobilized, a series of errors by several successive chief commanders appointed by the insurgent [Polish National Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_National_Government_(November_Uprising)) led to the defeat of its forces by the Russian army in 1831.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) Congress Poland lost its constitution and military, but formally remained a separate administrative unit within the Russian Empire.[[58\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_181–194-58)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Chopin%2C_by_Wodzinska.JPG/170px-Chopin%2C_by_Wodzinska.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Chopin,_by_Wodzinska.JPG)

[Chopin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frédéric_Chopin), a [Romantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romantic_music) composer of piano works, including many inspired by [Polish traditional dance music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_Poland#Traditional_music)

After the defeat of the November Uprising, thousands of former Polish combatants and other activists emigrated to [Western Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe). This phenomenon, known as the [Great Emigration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Emigration), soon dominated Polish political and intellectual life. Together with the leaders of the independence movement, the Polish community abroad included the greatest Polish literary and artistic minds, including the [Romantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanticism_in_Poland) [poets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Bards) [Adam Mickiewicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz), [Juliusz Słowacki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juliusz_Słowacki), [Cyprian Norwid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprian_Norwid), and the composer [Frédéric Chopin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frédéric_Chopin). In occupied and repressed Poland, some sought progress through nonviolent activism focused on education and economy, known as [organic work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_work); others, in cooperation with the emigrant circles, organized conspiracies and prepared for the next armed insurrection.[[59\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_208–231-59)

#### Revolts of the era of the Spring of Nations

The planned national uprising failed to materialize because the authorities in the partitions found out about secret preparations. The [Greater Poland uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_uprising_(1846)) ended in a fiasco in early 1846. In the [Kraków uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kraków_uprising) of February 1846,[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) patriotic action was combined with revolutionary demands, but the result was the incorporation of the [Free City of Cracow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_City_of_Cracow) into the Austrian Partition. The Austrian officials took advantage of peasant discontent and incited villagers against the noble-dominated insurgent units. This resulted in the [Galician slaughter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galician_slaughter) of 1846,[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) a large-scale rebellion of [serfs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serfdom) seeking relief from their post-feudal condition of [mandatory labor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serfdom_in_Poland) as practiced in *[folwarks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folwark)*. The uprising freed many from bondage and hastened decisions that led to the [abolition of Polish serfdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_serfdom_in_Poland) in the [Austrian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Empire) in 1848. A new wave of Polish involvement in revolutionary movements soon took place in the partitions and in other parts of Europe in the context of the [Spring of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848) revolutions of 1848 (e.g. [Józef Bem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Bem)'s participation in the [revolutions in Austria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Austrian_Empire) and [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1848)). The 1848 [German revolutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_revolutions_of_1848–49) precipitated the [Greater Poland uprising of 1848](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_uprising_(1848)),[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) in which peasants in the Prussian Partition, who were by then largely enfranchised, played a prominent role.[[60\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_232–287-60)

#### The Uprising of January 1863

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Romuald_Traugutt_111.PNG/170px-Romuald_Traugutt_111.PNG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Romuald_Traugutt_111.PNG)

[Romuald Traugutt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romuald_Traugutt), the last supreme commander of the [1863 Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_Uprising)

As a matter of continuous policy, the Russian autocracy kept assailing Polish national core values of language, religion and culture.[[61\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Burant_131–156-61) In consequence, despite the limited liberalization measures allowed in [Congress Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_Poland) under the rule of Tsar [Alexander II of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia), a renewal of popular liberation activities took place in 1860–1861. During large-scale demonstrations in Warsaw, Russian forces inflicted numerous casualties on the civilian participants. The "[Red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reds_(January_Uprising))", or [left-wing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics) faction of Polish activists, which promoted peasant enfranchisement and cooperated with Russian revolutionaries, became involved in immediate preparations for a national uprising. The "[White](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whites_(January_Uprising))", or [right-wing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_politics) faction, was inclined to cooperate with the Russian authorities and countered with partial reform proposals. In order to cripple the manpower potential of the Reds, [Aleksander Wielopolski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksander_Wielopolski), the conservative leader of the government of Congress Poland, arranged for a partial selective conscription of young Poles for the Russian army in the years 1862 and 1863.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) This action hastened the outbreak of hostilities. The [January Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_Uprising), joined and led after the initial period by the Whites, was fought by partisan units against an overwhelmingly advantaged enemy. The uprising lasted from January 1863 to the spring of 1864,[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) when [Romuald Traugutt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romuald_Traugutt), the last supreme commander of the insurgency, was captured by the tsarist police.[[62\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_287–311-62)[[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Biel,_czerwień,_czerń-63)

On 2 March 1864, the Russian authority, compelled by the uprising to compete for the loyalty of Polish peasants, officially published an [enfranchisement decree in Congress Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_serfdom_in_Poland) along the lines of an earlier land reform proclamation of the insurgents. The act created the conditions necessary for the development of the [capitalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalism) system on central Polish lands. At the time when most Poles realized the futility of armed resistance without external support, the various sections of Polish society were undergoing deep and far-reaching evolution in the areas of social, economic and cultural development.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53)[[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Biel,_czerwień,_czerń-63)[[64\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gierowski_311–318-64)

### Formation of modern Polish society under foreign rule (1864–1914)

#### Repression and organic work

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Boles%C5%82aw_Prus_%28ca._1905%29.jpg/170px-Boles%C5%82aw_Prus_%28ca._1905%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bolesław_Prus_(ca._1905).jpg)

[Bolesław Prus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolesław_Prus) (1847–1912), a leading novelist, journalist and [philosopher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_philosophy_in_Poland#Positivism) of Poland's [Positivism movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positivism_in_Poland)

The failure of the January Uprising in Poland caused a major psychological trauma and became a historic watershed; indeed, it sparked the development of modern [Polish nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_nationalism). The Poles, subjected within the territories under the Russian and Prussian administrations to still stricter controls and increased persecution, sought to preserve their identity in non-violent ways. After the uprising, Congress Poland was downgraded in official usage from the "Kingdom of Poland" to the "[Vistula Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vistula_Land)" and was more fully integrated into Russia proper, but not entirely obliterated. The [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language) and [German](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language) languages were imposed in all public communication, and the Catholic Church was not spared from severe repression. Public education was increasingly subjected to [Russification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russification) and [Germanisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanisation) measures. Illiteracy was reduced, most effectively in the Prussian partition, but education in the [Polish language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_language) was preserved mostly through unofficial efforts. The Prussian government pursued German colonization, including the purchase of Polish-owned land. On the other hand, the region of [Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)) (western Ukraine and southern Poland) experienced a gradual relaxation of authoritarian policies and even a Polish cultural revival. Economically and socially backward, it was under the milder rule of the [Austro-Hungarian Monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary) and from 1867 was increasingly allowed limited autonomy.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) *Stańczycy*, a conservative Polish pro-Austrian faction led by great land owners, dominated the Galician government. The [Polish Academy of Learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Learning) (an [academy of sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_of_sciences)) was founded in Kraków in 1872.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53)

Social activities termed "[organic work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_work)" consisted of self-help organizations that promoted economic advancement and work on improving the competitiveness of Polish-owned businesses, industrial, agricultural or other. New commercial methods of generating higher productivity were discussed and implemented through [trade associations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_association) and special interest groups, while Polish banking and cooperative financial institutions made the necessary business loans available. The other major area of effort in organic work was educational and intellectual development of the common people. Many libraries and reading rooms were established in small towns and villages, and numerous printed periodicals manifested the growing interest in popular education. Scientific and educational societies were active in a number of cities. Such activities were most pronounced in the Prussian Partition.[[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_182–187-65)[[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-66)

[Positivism in Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positivism_in_Poland) replaced Romanticism as the leading intellectual, social and literary trend.[[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_182–187-65)[[67\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_192–194-67) It reflected the ideals and values of the emerging urban [bourgeoisie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeoisie).[[68\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-68) Around 1890, the urban classes gradually abandoned the positivist ideas and came under the influence of modern pan-European [nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalism).[[69\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-69)

#### Economic development and social change

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Gierymski_Feast_of_trumpets_I.jpg/220px-Gierymski_Feast_of_trumpets_I.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gierymski_Feast_of_trumpets_I.jpg)

Many [Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland) emigrated from the Polish–Lithuanian lands in the late 19th and early 20th centuries, but most remained to form a large [ethnic minority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minority_group)

Under the partitioning powers, economic diversification and progress, including large-scale [industrialisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialisation), were introduced in the traditionally agrarian Polish lands, but this development turned out to be very uneven. Advanced agriculture was practiced in the Prussian Partition, except for [Upper Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Silesia), where the coal-mining industry created a large labor force. The densest network of railroads was built in German-ruled western Poland. In Russian Congress Poland, a striking growth of industry, railways and towns took place, all against the background of an extensive, but less productive agriculture.[[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_187–192,_199-70) The industrial initiative, capital and know-how were provided largely by entrepreneurs who were not ethnic Poles.[[71\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-71) Warsaw (a metallurgical center) and [Łódź](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Łódź) (a textiles center) grew rapidly, as did the total proportion of urban population, making the region the most economically advanced in the Russian Empire (industrial production exceeded agricultural production there by 1909). The coming of the railways spurred some industrial growth even in the vast Russian Partition territories outside of Congress Poland. The Austrian Partition was rural and poor, except for the industrialized [Cieszyn Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cieszyn_Silesia) area. [Galician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)) economic expansion after 1890 included oil extraction and resulted in the growth of [Lemberg (Lwów, Lviv)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lviv) and [Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kraków).[[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_187–192,_199-70)

Economic and social changes involving [land reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_reform) and industrialization, combined with the effects of foreign domination, altered the centuries-old social structure of Polish society. Among the newly emergent strata were wealthy industrialists and financiers, distinct from the traditional, but still critically important landed aristocracy. The [intelligentsia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligentsia), an educated, professional or business [middle class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_class), often originated from lower gentry, landless or alienated from their rural possessions, and from urban people. Many smaller agricultural enterprises based on serfdom did not survive the land reforms.[[72\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-72) The industrial [proletariat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proletariat), a new [underprivileged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privilege_(social_inequality)) class, was composed mainly of poor peasants or townspeople forced by deteriorating conditions to migrate and search for work in urban centers in their countries of origin or abroad. Millions of residents of the former Commonwealth of various [ethnic groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group) worked or settled in Europe and in [North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America) and [South America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_America).[[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_187–192,_199-70)

Social and economic changes were partial and gradual. The degree of industrialisation, relatively fast-paced in some areas, lagged behind the advanced regions of [Western Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe). The three partitions developed different economies and were more economically integrated with their mother states than with each other. In the Prussian Partition, for example, agricultural production depended heavily on the German market, whereas the industrial sector of Congress Poland relied more on the Russian market.[[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_187–192,_199-70)

#### Nationalism, socialism and other movements

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mariecurie.jpg/170px-Mariecurie.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mariecurie.jpg)

[Marie Curie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_Curie), discoverer of [radioactive elements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radioactive_decay)

In the 1870s–1890s, large-scale [socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism), [nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalism), [agrarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agrarianism) and other political movements of great ideological fervor became established in partitioned Poland and Lithuania, along with corresponding political parties to promote them. Of the major parties, the socialist [First Proletariat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proletariat_(party)) was founded in 1882, the Polish League (precursor of [National Democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Democracy_(Poland))) in 1887, the [Polish Social Democratic Party of Galicia and Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Social_Democratic_Party_of_Galicia) in 1890, the [Polish Socialist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Socialist_Party) in 1892, the [Marxist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism) [Social Democracy of the Kingdom of Poland and Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Democracy_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland_and_Lithuania) in 1893, the agrarian People's Party of Galicia in 1895 and the Jewish socialist [Bund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Jewish_Labour_Bund_in_Lithuania,_Poland_and_Russia) in 1897. [Christian democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_democracy) regional associations allied with the Catholic Church were also active; they united into the [Polish Christian Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Christian_Democratic_Party) in 1919.

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/RLuxemburgCpWz.jpg/170px-RLuxemburgCpWz.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:RLuxemburgCpWz.jpg)

[Rosa Luxemburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg), leader of the [Social Democracy of the Kingdom of Poland and Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Democracy_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland_and_Lithuania)

The main minority ethnic groups of the former Commonwealth, including [Ukrainians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainians), [Lithuanians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanians), [Belarusians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarusians) and [Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews), were getting involved in their own national movements and plans, which met with disapproval on the part of those Polish independence activists who counted on an eventual rebirth of the Commonwealth or the rise of a Commonwealth-inspired federal structure (a political movement referred to as [Prometheism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prometheism)).[[73\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_194–203-73)

Around the start of the 20th century, the [Young Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Poland) [cultural movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_movement), centered in [Austrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary) Galicia, took advantage of a milieu conducive to liberal expression in that region and was the source of Poland's finest artistic and literary productions.[[74\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_207–209-74) In this same era, [Marie Skłodowska Curie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_Curie), a pioneer [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionizing_radiation) scientist, performed her groundbreaking research in [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris).[[75\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_190-75)

#### The Revolution of 1905

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Roman_Dmowski_in_color.jpg/170px-Roman_Dmowski_in_color.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Roman_Dmowski_in_color.jpg)

[Roman Dmowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Dmowski)'s [National Democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Democracy_(Poland)) ideology proved highly influential in Polish politics. He favored the dominance of Polish-speaking Catholics in civic life without concern for the rights of ethnic minorities, in particular the Jews, whose emigration he advocated.

The [Revolution of 1905–1907 in Russian Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolution_in_the_Kingdom_of_Poland_(1905–07)),[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) the result of many years of pent-up political frustrations and stifled national ambitions, was marked by political maneuvering, strikes and rebellion. The revolt was part of much broader disturbances throughout the Russian Empire associated with the general [Revolution of 1905](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution). In Poland, the principal revolutionary figures were [Roman Dmowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Dmowski) and [Józef Piłsudski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Piłsudski). Dmowski was associated with the right-wing nationalist movement [National Democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Democracy_(Poland)), whereas Piłsudski was associated with the [Polish Socialist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Socialist_Party). As the authorities re-established control within the Russian Empire, the revolt in Congress Poland, placed under martial law, withered as well, partially as a result of tsarist concessions in the areas of national and workers' rights, including Polish representation in the newly created Russian [Duma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Duma_(Russian_Empire)). The collapse of the revolt in the Russian Partition, coupled with intensified Germanization in the Prussian Partition, left [Austrian Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia_and_Lodomeria) as the territory where Polish patriotic action was most likely to flourish.[[76\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_203–208-76)

In the Austrian Partition, Polish culture was openly cultivated, and in the Prussian Partition, there were high levels of education and living standards, but the Russian Partition remained of primary importance for the Polish nation and its aspirations. About 15.5 million Polish-speakers lived in the territories most densely populated by Poles: the western part of the Russian Partition, the Prussian Partition and the western Austrian Partition. Ethnically Polish settlement spread over a large area further to the east, including its greatest concentration in the [Vilnius Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilnius_Region), amounted to only over 20% of that number.[[77\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_208–216-77)

Polish paramilitary organizations oriented toward independence, such as the [Union of Active Struggle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_of_Active_Struggle), were formed in 1908–1914, mainly in Galicia. The Poles were divided and their political parties fragmented on the eve of [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I), with Dmowski's National Democracy (pro-[Entente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I)) and Piłsudski's faction assuming opposing positions.[[77\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_208–216-77)[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)

### World War I and the issue of Poland's independence

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Pilsudski_in_Otwock.jpg/260px-Pilsudski_in_Otwock.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pilsudski_in_Otwock.jpg)

"The Commandant" [Józef Piłsudski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Piłsudski) with his [legionaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Legions_in_World_War_I) in 1915

The outbreak of [World War I in the Polish lands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Poland_during_World_War_I) offered Poles unexpected hopes for achieving independence as a result of the turbulence that engulfed the empires of the partitioning powers. All three of the monarchies that had benefited from the partition of Polish territories (Germany, Austria and Russia) were dissolved by the end of the war, and many of their territories were dispersed into new political units. At the start of the war, the Poles found themselves conscripted into the armies of the partitioning powers in a war that was not theirs. Furthermore, they were frequently forced to fight each other, since the armies of Germany and Austria were allied against Russia. Piłsudski's paramilitary units stationed in [Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)) were turned into the [Polish Legions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Legions_in_World_War_I) in 1914 and as a part of the [Austro-Hungarian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Army) fought on the Russian front until 1917, when the formation was disbanded.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) Piłsudski, who refused demands that his men fight under German command, was arrested and imprisoned by the Germans and became a heroic symbol of Polish nationalism.[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)[[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_279–290-79)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Ignacy_Paderewski_02.jpg/170px-Ignacy_Paderewski_02.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ignacy_Paderewski_02.jpg)

[Ignacy Paderewski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Jan_Paderewski) was a pianist and a statesman

Due to a series of German victories on the [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)), the area of [Congress Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_Poland) became occupied by the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers) of Germany and Austria;[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) Warsaw was captured by the Germans on 5 August 1915. In the [Act of 5th November](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_5th_November) 1916, a fresh incarnation of the [Kingdom of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1917–1918)) (*Królestwo Regencyjne*) was proclaimed by Germany and Austria on formerly Russian-controlled territories,[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53) within the German *[Mitteleuropa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitteleuropa)* scheme. The sponsor states were never able to agree on a candidate to assume the throne, however; rather, it was governed in turn by German and Austrian governor-generals, a [Provisional Council of State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisional_Council_of_State), and a [Regency Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regency_Council_(Poland)). This increasingly autonomous puppet state existed until November 1918, when it was replaced by the newly established [Republic of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic). The existence of this "kingdom" and its planned Polish army had a positive effect on the Polish national efforts on the [Allied side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_Entente), but in the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk) of March 1918 the victorious in the east [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Empire) imposed harsh conditions on defeated Russia and ignored Polish interests.[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)[[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_279–290-79)[[80\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Versailles-80) Toward the end of the war, the German authorities engaged in massive, purposeful devastation of industrial and other economic potential of Polish lands in order to impoverish the country, a likely future competitor of Germany.[[81\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-81)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Polish_Regents_1916.jpg/220px-Polish_Regents_1916.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Polish_Regents_1916.jpg)

The Regency Council of the [Kingdom of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1917–1918)) in 1918. The "Kingdom" was established to entice Poles to cooperate with the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers).

The independence of Poland had been campaigned for in Russia and in the West by Dmowski and in the West by [Ignacy Jan Paderewski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Jan_Paderewski). Tsar [Nicholas II of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia), and then the leaders of the [February Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_Revolution) and the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution) of 1917, installed governments who declared in turn their support for Polish independence.[[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_279–290-79)[[d1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_d1none) In 1917, France formed the [Blue Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Army_(Poland)) (placed under [Józef Haller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Haller)) that comprised about 70,000 Poles by the end of the war, including men captured from German and Austrian units and 20,000 volunteers from the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States). There was also a 30,000-men strong Polish anti-German army in Russia. Dmowski, operating from Paris as head of the [Polish National Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_National_Committee_(1917–19)) (KNP), became the spokesman for Polish nationalism in the Allied camp. On the initiative of [Woodrow Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson)'s [Fourteen Points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteen_Points), Polish independence was officially endorsed by the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I) in June 1918.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53)[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)[[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_279–290-79)[[c1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_c1none)

In all, about two million Poles served in the war, counting both sides, and about 400–450,000 died. Much of the fighting on the Eastern Front took place in Poland, and civilian casualties and devastation were high.[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)[[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-82)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ignacy_Daszy%C5%84ski_1915.jpg/170px-Ignacy_Daszy%C5%84ski_1915.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ignacy_Daszyński_1915.jpg)

[Ignacy Daszyński](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Daszyński)

The final push for independence of Poland took place on the ground in October–November 1918. Near the end of the war, [Austro-Hungarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary) and German units were being disarmed, and the Austrian army's collapse freed [Cieszyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cieszyn) and [Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kraków) at the end of October. [Lviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lviv) was then contested in the [Polish–Ukrainian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Ukrainian_War) of 1918–1919. [Ignacy Daszyński](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Daszyński) headed the first short-lived independent Polish government in [Lublin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lublin) from 7 November, the leftist Provisional People's Government of the Republic of Poland, proclaimed as a democracy. Germany, now defeated, was forced by the Allies to stand down its large military forces in Poland. Overtaken by the [German Revolution of 1918–1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918–19) at home, the Germans released Piłsudski from prison. He arrived in Warsaw on 10 November and was granted extensive authority by the [Regency Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regency_Council_(Poland)); Piłsudski's authority was also recognized by the Lublin government.[[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_xxi-53)[[b1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_b1none) On 22 November, he became the temporary head of state. Piłsudski was held by many in high regard, but was resented by the right-wing National Democrats. The emerging Polish state was internally divided, heavily war-damaged and economically dysfunctional.[[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_217–222-78)[[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_II_279–290-79)

## Second Polish Republic (1918–1939)

### Securing national borders, war with Soviet Russia

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Powstanie_wielkopolskie_1919.jpg/220px-Powstanie_wielkopolskie_1919.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Powstanie_wielkopolskie_1919.jpg)

The [Greater Poland Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_uprising_(1918–1919)), a war with Germany, erupted in December 1918

After more than a century of foreign rule, Poland regained its independence at the end of [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I) as one of the outcomes of the negotiations that took place at the [Paris Peace Conference of 1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919).[[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-83) The [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles) that emerged from the conference set up an independent Polish nation with an outlet to the sea, but left some of its boundaries to be decided by plebiscites. The largely German-inhabited [Free City of Danzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_City_of_Danzig) was granted a separate status that guaranteed its use as a port by Poland. In the end, the settlement of the German-Polish border turned out to be a prolonged and convoluted process. The dispute helped engender the [Greater Poland Uprising of 1918–1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_uprising_(1918–1919)), the three [Silesian uprisings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings) of 1919–1921, the [East Prussian plebiscite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1920_East_Prussian_plebiscite) of 1920, the [Upper Silesia plebiscite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Silesia_plebiscite) of 1921 and the 1922 Silesian Convention in [Geneva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva).[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[85\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-85)[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)

Other boundaries were settled by war and subsequent treaties. A total of six border wars were fought in 1918–1921, including the [Polish–Czechoslovak border conflicts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Czechoslovak_border_conflicts) over [Cieszyn Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cieszyn_Silesia) in January 1919.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Polish-soviet_war_1920_Polish_defences_near_Milosna%2C_August.jpg/220px-Polish-soviet_war_1920_Polish_defences_near_Milosna%2C_August.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Polish-soviet_war_1920_Polish_defences_near_Milosna,_August.jpg)

[Polish–Soviet War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Soviet_War), [defenses near Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920)), August 1920

As distressing as these border conflicts were, the [Polish–Soviet War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Soviet_War) of 1919–1921 was the most important series of military actions of the era. Piłsudski had entertained far-reaching anti-Russian cooperative designs in Eastern Europe, and in 1919 the Polish forces pushed eastward into Lithuania, Belarus and Ukraine by taking advantage of the Russian preoccupation with a [civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War), but they were soon confronted with the [Soviet westward offensive of 1918–1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_westward_offensive_of_1918–19). Western Ukraine was already a theater of the [Polish–Ukrainian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Ukrainian_War), which eliminated the proclaimed [West Ukrainian People's Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Ukrainian_People's_Republic) in July 1919. In the autumn of 1919, Piłsudski rejected urgent pleas from the former [Entente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I) powers to support [Anton Denikin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anton_Denikin)'s [White movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_movement) in its advance on Moscow.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84) The Polish–Soviet War proper began with the Polish [Kiev Offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev_Offensive_(1920)) in April 1920.[[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-87) Allied with the [Directorate of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directorate_of_Ukraine) of the [Ukrainian People's Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_People's_Republic), the Polish armies had advanced past [Vilnius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilnius), [Minsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minsk) and Kiev by June.[[88\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-88) At that time, a massive Soviet counter-offensive pushed the Poles out of most of Ukraine. On the northern front, the Soviet army reached the outskirts of Warsaw in early August. A Soviet triumph and the quick end of Poland seemed inevitable. However, the Poles scored a stunning victory at the [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920)). Afterwards, more [Polish military successes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Niemen_River) followed, and the Soviets had to pull back. They left swathes of territory populated largely by Belarusians or Ukrainians to Polish rule. The new eastern boundary was finalized by the [Peace of Riga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Riga) in March 1921.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)[[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-89)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Daszynski_and_Witos.jpg/220px-Daszynski_and_Witos.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Daszynski_and_Witos.jpg)

[Wincenty Witos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wincenty_Witos) (right) and Ignacy Daszyński headed a wartime cabinet in 1920. Witos was an [agrarian party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People's_Party_"Piast"_(1913–31)) leader and a centrist politician, later [persecuted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brest_trials) under the [Sanation regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanation).

The defeat of the Russian armies forced [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin) and the Soviet leadership to postpone their strategic objective of linking up with the German and other European revolutionary leftist collaborators to spread [communist revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_revolution). Lenin also hoped for generating support for the [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army) in Poland, which failed to materialize.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wojciech_Korfanty.PNG/170px-Wojciech_Korfanty.PNG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wojciech_Korfanty.PNG)

[Wojciech Korfanty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wojciech_Korfanty) [fought for a Polish Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings) and was the leader of the [Polish Christian Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Christian_Democratic_Party)

Piłsudski's seizure of Vilnius in October 1920 (known as [Żeligowski's Mutiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Żeligowski's_Mutiny)) was a nail in the coffin of the already poor [Lithuania–Poland relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania–Poland_relations) that had been strained by the [Polish–Lithuanian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Lithuanian_War) of 1919–1920; both states would remain hostile to one another for the remainder of the [interwar period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interwar_period).[[90\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-90) Piłsudski's concept of [Intermarium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intermarium) (an East European federation of states inspired by the tradition of the multiethnic [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish–Lithuanian_Commonwealth) that would include a hypothetical multinational successor state to the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania))[[91\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Snyder_60-65-91) had the fatal flaw of being incompatible with his assumption of Polish domination, which would amount to an encroachment on the neighboring peoples' lands and aspirations. At the time of rising national movements, the plan thus ceased being a feature of Poland's politics.[[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Prazmowska_164-172-92)[[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-93)[[94\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Snyder_57-60,_62-94)[[a\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_anone) A larger federated structure was also opposed by Dmowski's National Democrats. Their representative at the [Peace of Riga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Riga) talks, [Stanisław Grabski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanisław_Grabski), opted for leaving Minsk, [Berdychiv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berdychiv), [Kamianets-Podilskyi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi) and the surrounding areas on the Soviet side of the border. The National Democrats did not want to assume the lands they considered politically undesirable, as such territorial enlargement would result in a reduced proportion of citizens who were ethnically Polish.[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)[[95\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-95)[[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Snyder_64-65,_68-69-96)

The Peace of Riga settled the eastern border by preserving for Poland a substantial portion of the old Commonwealth's eastern territories at the cost of partitioning the lands of the former Grand Duchy of Lithuania (Lithuania and Belarus) and Ukraine.[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)[[97\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Snyder_63-69-97)[[98\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_147-98) The Ukrainians ended up with no state of their own and felt betrayed by the Riga arrangements; their resentment gave rise to extreme nationalism and anti-Polish hostility.[[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Snyder_139-144-99) The [Kresy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kresy) (or borderland) territories in the east won by 1921 would form the basis for a swap arranged and carried out by the Soviets in 1943–1945, who at that time [compensated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_immediately_after_World_War_II) the re-emerging Polish state for the eastern lands lost to the Soviet Union with [conquered areas of eastern Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovered_Territories).[[100\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121,_73-80-100)

The successful outcome of the Polish–Soviet War gave Poland a false sense of its prowess as a self-sufficient military power and encouraged the government to try to resolve international problems through imposed unilateral solutions.[[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Prazmowska_164-172-92)[[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_232-101) The territorial and ethnic policies of the interwar period contributed to bad relations with most of Poland's neighbors and uneasy cooperation with more distant centers of power, especially [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France) and [Great Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom).[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)[[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Prazmowska_164-172-92)[[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_232-101)

### Democratic politics (1918–1926)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Narutowicz.jpg/220px-Narutowicz.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Narutowicz.jpg)

[Bier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bier) of [Gabriel Narutowicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Narutowicz), the first President of Poland, who was assassinated in 1922

Among the chief difficulties faced by the government of the new Polish republic was the lack of an integrated infrastructure among the formerly separate partitions, a deficiency that disrupted industry, transportation, trade, and other areas.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

The first [Polish legislative election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1919_Polish_legislative_election) for the re-established [Sejm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sejm) (national parliament) took place in January 1919. A temporary [Small Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Constitution_of_1919) was passed by the body the following month.[[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Lukowski_223-102)

The rapidly growing population of Poland within its new boundaries was three-fourths agricultural and one-fourth urban; Polish was the primary language of only two thirds of the inhabitants of the new country. The minorities had very little voice in the government. The permanent [March Constitution of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_Constitution_of_Poland) was adopted in March 1921. At the insistence of the National Democrats, who were concerned about how aggressively Józef Piłsudski might exercise presidential powers if he were elected to office, the constitution mandated limited prerogatives for the presidency.[[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_115-121-86)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Grabski_1925.jpg/170px-W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Grabski_1925.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Władysław_Grabski_1925.jpg)

[Władysław Grabski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Władysław_Grabski) reformed the currency and introduced the [Polish zloty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_zloty) to replace the [marka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_marka)

The proclamation of the March Constitution was followed by a short and turbulent period of constitutional order and parliamentary democracy that lasted until 1926. The legislature remained fragmented, without stable majorities, and governments changed frequently. The open-minded [Gabriel Narutowicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Narutowicz) was elected president constitutionally (without a popular vote) by the [National Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_(Poland)) in 1922. However, members of the nationalist right-wing faction did not regard his elevation as legitimate. They viewed Narutowicz rather as a traitor whose election was pushed through by the votes of alien minorities. Narutowicz and his supporters were subjected to an intense harassment campaign, and the president was assassinated on 16 December 1922, after serving only five days in office.[[103\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Hart_121-123-103)

[Land reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_reform) measures were passed in 1919 and 1925 under pressure from an impoverished peasantry. They were partially implemented, but resulted in the parcellation of only 20% of the great agricultural estates.[[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Ziemia_dla_chłopów-104) Poland endured numerous economic calamities and disruptions in the early 1920s, including waves of workers' strikes such as the [1923 Kraków riot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1923_Kraków_riot). The [German–Polish customs war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German–Polish_customs_war), initiated by Germany in 1925, was one of the most damaging external factors that put a strain on Poland's economy.[[105\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-105)[[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_307,_308-106) On the other hand, there were also signs of progress and stabilization, for example a critical reform of finances carried out by the competent government of [Władysław Grabski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Władysław_Grabski), which lasted almost two years. Certain other achievements of the democratic period having to do with the management of governmental and civic institutions necessary to the functioning of the reunited state and nation were too easily overlooked. Lurking on the sidelines was a disgusted army officer corps unwilling to subject itself to civilian control, but ready to follow the retired Piłsudski, who was highly popular with Poles and just as dissatisfied with the Polish system of government as his former colleagues in the military.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[103\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Hart_121-123-103)

### Piłsudski's coup and the Sanation Era (1926–1935)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Pi%C5%82sudski_May_1926.jpg/220px-Pi%C5%82sudski_May_1926.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Piłsudski_May_1926.jpg)

Piłsudski's [May Coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Coup_(Poland)) of 1926 defined Poland's political reality in the years leading to World War II

On 12 May 1926, Piłsudski staged the [May Coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Coup_(Poland)), a military overthrow of the civilian government mounted against President [Stanisław Wojciechowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanisław_Wojciechowski) and the troops loyal to the legitimate government. Hundreds died in fratricidal fighting.[[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_312-107) Piłsudski was supported by several leftist factions who ensured the success of his coup by blocking the railway transportation of government forces.[[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Hart_123-127-108)[[b1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_b1none) He also had the support of the conservative great landowners, a move that left the right-wing National Democrats as the only major social force opposed to the takeover.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[109\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-109)[[l\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_lnone)

Following the coup, the new regime initially respected many parliamentary formalities, but gradually tightened its control and abandoned pretenses. The [Centrolew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrolew), a coalition of center-left parties, was formed in 1929, and in 1930 called for the "abolition of dictatorship". In 1930, the Sejm was dissolved and a number of opposition deputies were imprisoned at the [Brest Fortress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brest_Fortress). Five thousand political opponents were arrested ahead of the [Polish legislative election of 1930](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1930_Polish_legislative_election),[[110\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Brzoza_Sowa_309-110) which was rigged to award a majority of seats to the pro-regime [Nonpartisan Bloc for Cooperation with the Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonpartisan_Bloc_for_Cooperation_with_the_Government) (BBWR).[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Wybrać,_jak_trzeba-111)[[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gwałt_i_ratunek-112)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Rydz_Smigly_Bulawa1.jpg/170px-Rydz_Smigly_Bulawa1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rydz_Smigly_Bulawa1.jpg)

President [Ignacy Mościcki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Mościcki) and Marshal [Edward Rydz-Śmigły](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Rydz-Śmigły) were among top leaders of [Sanation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanation) Poland

The authoritarian [Sanation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanation) regime ("sanation" meant to denote "healing") that Piłsudski led until his death in 1935 (and would remain in place until 1939) reflected the dictator's evolution from his center-left past to conservative alliances.[[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Wybrać,_jak_trzeba-111) Political institutions and parties were allowed to function, but the electoral process was manipulated and those not willing to cooperate submissively were subjected to repression. From 1930, persistent opponents of the regime, many of the leftist persuasion, were imprisoned and subjected to [staged legal processes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Show_trial) with harsh sentences, such as the [Brest trials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brest_trials), or else detained in the [Bereza Kartuska prison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bereza_Kartuska_prison) and similar camps for political prisoners. About three thousand were detained without trial at different times at the Bereza [internment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment) camp between 1934 and 1939. In 1936 for example, 369 activists were taken there, including 342 [Polish communists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Poland).[[113\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Bereza,_Polski_obóz_koncentracyjny-113) Rebellious peasants staged riots in 1932, 1933 and the [1937 peasant strike in Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1937_peasant_strike_in_Poland). Other civil disturbances were caused by striking industrial workers (e.g. events of the "Bloody Spring" of 1936), nationalist Ukrainians[[p\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_pnone) and the activists of the incipient Belarusian movement. All became targets of ruthless police-military pacification.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[114\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-114)[[115\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Brzoza_Sowa_322–329-115)[[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Brzoza_Sowa_353–359-116)[[y\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_ynone) Besides sponsoring political repression, the regime fostered [Józef Piłsudski's cult of personality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Piłsudski's_cult_of_personality) that had already existed long before he assumed dictatorial powers.

Piłsudski signed the [Soviet–Polish Non-Aggression Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet–Polish_Non-Aggression_Pact) in 1932 and the [German–Polish declaration of non-aggression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German–Polish_declaration_of_non-aggression) in 1934,[[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Hart_123-127-108) but in 1933 he insisted that there was no threat from the East or West and said that Poland's politics were focused on becoming fully independent without serving foreign interests.[[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-117) He initiated the policy of maintaining an equal distance and an adjustable middle course regarding the two great neighbors, later continued by [Józef Beck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Beck).[[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-118) Piłsudski kept personal control of the army, but it was poorly equipped, poorly trained and had poor preparations in place for possible future conflicts.[[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-119) His only war plan was a defensive war against a Soviet invasion.[[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-120)[[r\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#endnote_rnone) The slow modernization after Piłsudski's death fell far behind the progress made by Poland's neighbors and measures to protect the western border, discontinued by Piłsudski from 1926, were not undertaken until March 1939.[[121\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-121)

Sanation deputies in the Sejm used a parliamentary maneuver to abolish the democratic [March Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_Constitution_of_Poland) and push through a more authoritarian [April Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_Constitution_of_Poland) in 1935; it reduced the powers of the Sejm, which Piłsudski despised.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84) The process and the resulting document were seen as illegitimate by the anti-Sanation opposition, but during World War II, the [Polish government-in-exile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile) recognized the April Constitution in order to uphold the legal continuity of the Polish state.[[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-122)

Between 1932 and 1933 [Piłsudski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Piłsudski) and [Beck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Józef_Beck) initiated several incidents along the borders with Germany and [Danzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_City_of_Danzig), both to test whether Western powers would protect the [Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles) arrangements (on which Polish security depended), and as preparation for a [preventative war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preventative_war) against Germany. At the same time they sent emissaries to London and Paris, looking for their support in stopping [Germany's rearmament effort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_rearmament). An invasion to Danzig by Poland was scheduled for April 21, 1933, but the amassing of troops was discovered and the invasion was postponed. At the time an invasion by Poland would have posed a serious military threat to Germany, but with the British rejecting the idea (in favor of the [Four-Power Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four-Power_Pact)), and with wavering support from the French, the Poles had eventually reneged on the idea of invasion. Between 1933 and 1934 Germany would increase its armament expenditures by 68%, and by January 1934 the two powers would sign a ten-year [non-aggression pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German–Polish_declaration_of_non-aggression).[[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Crockett_2009-123)

When Marshal Piłsudski died in 1935, he retained the support of dominant sections of Polish society even though he never risked testing his popularity in an honest election. His regime was dictatorial, but at that time only [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia) remained democratic in all of the regions neighboring Poland. Historians have taken widely divergent views of the meaning and consequences of the coup Piłsudski perpetrated and his personal rule that followed.[[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Gwałt_i_ratunek-112)

### Social and economic trends of the interwar period

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eugeniusz_Kwiatkowski.PNG/170px-Eugeniusz_Kwiatkowski.PNG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Eugeniusz_Kwiatkowski.PNG)

[Eugeniusz Kwiatkowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugeniusz_Kwiatkowski) promoted Poland's [Central Industrial Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Industrial_Region_(Poland))

Independence stimulated the development of [Polish culture in the Interbellum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_culture_in_the_Interbellum) and intellectual achievement was high. Warsaw, whose population almost doubled between World War I and World War II, was a restless, burgeoning metropolis. It outpaced Kraków, [Lwów](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lviv) and [Wilno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilnius), the other major population centers of the country.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

Mainstream Polish society was not affected by the repressions of the Sanation authorities overall;[[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-Heart_126-124) many Poles enjoyed relative stability, and the economy improved markedly between 1926 and 1929, only to become caught up in the global [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression).[[125\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-125) After 1929, the country's [industrial production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_production) and [gross national income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_national_income) slumped by about 50%.[[126\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-126)

The Great Depression brought low prices for farmers and unemployment for workers. Social tensions increased, including rising [antisemitism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism). A major economic transformation and multi-year state plan to achieve national industrial development, as embodied in the [Central Industrial Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Industrial_Region_(Poland)) initiative launched in 1936, was led by Minister [Eugeniusz Kwiatkowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugeniusz_Kwiatkowski). Motivated primarily by the need for a native [arms industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_industry), the initiative was in progress at the time of the outbreak of World War II. Kwiatkowski was also the main architect of the earlier [Gdynia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gdynia) seaport project.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)[[127\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-127)

Portraits of poets by [Witkacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanisław_Ignacy_Witkiewicz)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Witkacy_Maria_P_J.jpg/135px-Witkacy_Maria_P_J.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Witkacy_Maria_P_J.jpg)

[Maria Pawlikowska-Jasnorzewska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maria_Pawlikowska-Jasnorzewska)

[![img](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Witkacy_Julian_Tuwim.jpg/128px-Witkacy_Julian_Tuwim.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Witkacy_Julian_Tuwim.jpg)

[Julian Tuwim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julian_Tuwim)

The prevalent in political circles [nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalism) was fueled by the large size of Poland's minority populations and their separate agendas. According to the language criterion of the [Polish census of 1931](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_census_of_1931), the Poles constituted 69% of the population, Ukrainians 15%, Jews (defined as speakers of the [Yiddish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yiddish) language) 8.5%, Belarusians 4.7%, Germans 2.2%, Lithuanians 0.25%, Russians 0.25% and Czechs 0.09%, with some geographical areas dominated by a particular minority. In time, the ethnic conflicts intensified, and the Polish state grew less tolerant of the interests of its national minorities. In interwar Poland, compulsory free general education substantially reduced illiteracy rates, but discrimination was practiced in a way that resulted in a dramatic decrease in the number of [Ukrainian language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_language) schools and official restrictions on Jewish attendance at selected schools in the late 1930s.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

The population grew steadily, reaching 35 million in 1939. However, the overall economic situation in the interwar period was one of [stagnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_stagnation). There was little money for investment inside Poland, and few foreigners were interested in investing there.[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84) Total industrial production barely increased between 1913 and 1939 (within the area delimited by the 1939 borders), but because of population growth (from 26.3 million in 1919 to 34.8 million in 1939),[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84) the *per capita* output actually decreased by 18%.[[128\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-128)

Conditions in the predominant agricultural sector kept deteriorating between 1929 and 1939, which resulted in rural unrest and a progressive radicalization of the Polish peasant movement that became increasingly inclined toward militant anti-state activities. It was firmly repressed by the authorities. According to [Norman Davies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norman_Davies), the failures of the Sanation regime (combined with the objective economic realities) caused a radicalization of the Polish masses by the end of the 1930s, but he warns against drawing parallels with the incomparably more repressive regimes of [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany) or the [Stalinist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalinism) [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union).[[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Poland&printable=yes#cite_note-playground_291–321-84)

### Final Sanation years (1935–1939)
